Removal of Scars: Use eagle's arrow white combined with human essence, apply for three days.
Another formula: Two taels of eagle's arrow white, one and a half taels of stiff silkworm ground into powder, mix with honey and apply.
Another formula: One tael each of eagle's arrow white and white attachia ground into powder, mix with vinegar and apply three to five times a day until the scar disappears.

Warts on body and face: Every month during the full moon at the child hour, sweep the warts with a broom seven times.
Another formula: Frequent application of cow saliva will cause them to fall off.
Another formula: Grind equal parts of calamine, borax, rust, and musk, and apply three times until they fall off.

Freckles and facial blemishes: On the seventh day of the seventh month, obtain bee larvae, soak in water and wine to filter the juice, mix with ground powdered flower and apply.

Tattoo removal: Apply white horse urine, then mix with leech powder and smear.

Red spots on body and face: Regularly rub with heated silver, and over time they will disappear.

(Black spots): Use the kernels of plums, remove the skin and grind finely, mix with egg white to create a thin paste, apply until dawn and then wash off with starch water; apply powdered flower afterward, it will take effect in five or six days. Avoid exposure to wind.
Another formula: Burn the clothing of a filial son to ash and apply.[57p]

　　粉刺黑斑：五月五日，收带根益母草紫花者，晒干烧灰，以商陆根捣自然汁，加酸酢搜和灰作饼，炭火煅过收之，半年方用，入面药。【《闺阁事宜》，下同。】　　又方：五月五日，采益母草根苗具者，勿令着土，暴干捣罗，以面水和成团如鸡子大，再暴干；仍作一炉，四旁开窍，上下置火，安药中央，大火烧一炊久，即去大火，留小火养之，勿令火绝，经一复时出之，瓷器中研，治筛，再研三日收用，如澡豆法，日用。一方，每十两加滑石一两，胭脂一钱。
　　藜茎灰、荻灰、蒿灰等分，水和蒸取汁煎膏，点赘黑子，蚀恶肉。 【时珍】
　　消灭瘢痕：以猪脂三斤，饲乌鸡一只，三日后取矢，同白芷、当归各一两，煎十沸去渣，入鹰矢白半两调敷。【《外台》】
　　雀卵面疱：鸡卵酢浸坏，取出敷之。 【《圣惠》，下同。】[58p]

Acne and Dark Spots: On the fifth day of the fifth month, gather the roots and flowering tops of motherwort, dry them in the sun and burn them to ashes. Mix the ashes with the juice of the root of the merchant's gall, add sour vinegar to form cakes, and bake them over charcoal until done. They can be used after six months, incorporated into the internal medicine.

Another Method: On the fifth day of the fifth month, gather the root and sprouts of motherwort, ensuring they do not touch the soil. Dry them violently and crush them through a sieve. Mix with water to form balls the size of a chicken egg, then dry them again. Prepare a furnace, opening vents on the sides, place wood both above and below, and put the medicinal preparation in the center. Use a high flame to cook it for a while, then reduce to a low flame to maintain the heat without extinguishing it. After one cycle, remove it, grind in porcelain, treat through a sieve, and grind again for three days before use as with soap beans, daily applied. For one method, add one tael of talc and one qian of rouge for every ten taels.

Mix equal parts of broom reed ash, sedge ash, and mugwort ash, add water, steam to extract juice, and boil down to a thick paste. Apply to moles and sores to corrode bad flesh.

Scar Removal: Use three jin of pig fat, feed it to a black chicken, then after three days, take the droppings, mix with one tael each of white atractylodes and angelica, simmer until boiling ten times, strain out the dregs, and mix with half a tael of eagle droppings for topical application.

Pustules resembling bird eggs: Soak chicken egg vinegar until spoiled, take it out and apply.[58p]

　　消灭瘢痕：鸡子五七枚，煮熟取黄炒黑拭涂，日三，久久自灭。
　　面疱：鹰矢白二分，胡粉一分，蜜和敷之。 【《外台》】
　　　　针灸

　　《灵枢经》曰：手太阳之别，名曰支正，上腕五寸。虚则生疣，小者如指痂疥，取之所别也。　　《甲乙经》曰：振寒热颈项肿，实则肘挛，头项痛狂易，虚则生疣，小者痂疥，支正主之。　　瘿，天窻 【一作天容】 及臑会主之。　　瘿瘤，气舍主之。
　　《千金方》曰：瘿，恶气，灸天府五十壮。 【《千金翼》作胸堂百壮】　　瘿，上气短气，灸肺俞百壮。
　　瘿，上气胸满，灸云门五十壮。
　　瘿，劳气，灸冲阳随年壮。
　　瘿气面肿，灸通天五十壮。
　　瘿，灸天髎三百壮，横三间一寸灸之；又灸中封随年壮，在两足趺上曲内宛宛中。　　诸瘿，灸肩髃左右相当宛宛处，男左十八壮，右十七壮；女右十八壮，左十七壮。或再三，取瘥止。　　又法：灸风池百壮，侠项两边。[59p]

Eliminating Scars: Take five to seven eggs, boil them, take the yolks, fry them black and apply them three times a day; over time, they will disappear by themselves.

For Facial Acne: Mix two parts eagle's quill, one part white powder, and honey; apply this mixture.

Acupuncture and Moxibustion

The "Lingshu" states: The hand sun meridian diverges at a point called Zhi Zheng, located five inches above the wrist. When deficient, warts arise, small ones resembling finger scabs. This divergence defines where to treat. The "Jia Yi Jing" states: For cold and heat causing neck swelling, when full it indicates elbow constriction, leading to headache and delirium; when deficient, it results in warts and small scabs, treated at Zhi Zheng. Enlargements like goiters, referred to as Tian Kwang (or Tian Rong), are treated at the joint. Goiters or nodules caused by Qi stagnation are treated at the corresponding meridian.

The "Qian Jin Fang" states: For goiters, caused by harmful Qi, moxibustion is to be applied at Tian Fu fifty times. Goiters accompanied by shortness of breath require moxibustion at Lung Shu a hundred times. Goiters causing chest fullness should receive moxibustion at Yun Men fifty times. For goiters related to fatigue, apply moxibustion at Chong Yang annually. In cases of face swelling due to goiters, moxibustion at Tong Tian fifty times is advised.

Goiters should be treated with moxibustion at Tian Liao three hundred times, horizontally one inch apart; additionally, moxibustion at Zhong Feng should be done annually, specifically at the inner curves beneath both feet. For all goiters, perform moxibustion at Jian Yu on both sides equivalently; for men, eighteen times on the left side and seventeen times on the right; for women, seventeen times on the left side and eighteen times on the right. Repeat several times until recovery is noted.

Additionally, apply moxibustion at Feng Chi a hundred times on both sides of the neck.[59p]

　　又法：灸两耳后发际一百壮。
　　又法：灸头冲 【一作颈】 ，在伸两手直向前，令臂着头对鼻所注处灸之，各随年壮。【《千金翼》，名臂臑。】　　天府、臑会、气舍，主瘿瘤气咽肿。　　脑户、通天、消泺、天突，主颈有大气。　　通天主瘿，灸五十壮。胸堂、羊屎灸一百壮。　　《本事方》曰：治果报面生赘瘤方，用艾丸灸十壮，即用酢磨硫黄涂纸上，剪如螺蛳掩子大，贴所灸处，更用膏药重贴，二日一换，候痒，挤出脓如菉豆粉即愈。【按硫黄，罗谦甫作雄黄。】　　《李杲十书》曰：诸瘿恶气，天府七七壮，冲阳随年壮。
　　　　医案
　　《儒门事亲》曰：新寨妇人年四十余，有瘿三瓣，戴人令以咸吐之，三涌三汗三下，瘿已半消；次服化瘿之药，遂大消。夫病在上者皆宜吐，亦自有消息之法耳。[60p]

Another method: Moxibustion at the hairline behind both ears with a hundred dosages.
Another method: Moxibustion at the head’s vertex (or neck); stretch both arms straight forward and perform moxibustion where the arms touch the head, directed towards the nose, with dosages corresponding to one's age and strength.

The Tianfu, Nao hui, Qishe points are for treating goiters and swelling in the throat.
The Naohud, Tongtian, Xiaolu, Tiantu points are for addressing significant conditions in the neck.
Tongtian is for goiters; apply fifty dosages of moxibustion.
For Xiong Tang and Yangshi, apply one hundred dosages of moxibustion.

The "Ben Shi Fang" states: For treating growths on the face, use moxa balls with ten dosages; then take vinegar to grind sulfur, apply it to paper cut in the size of a snail shell cover, and adhere it to the moxibustion site. Reinforce with a plaster, change it every two days, wait for itching, then squeeze out pus resembling powdered peas; this treatment leads to healing. [Note: Sulfur is also referred to as Xiong Huang by Luo Qianfu.]

The "Ten Books of Li Gao" states: For all foul energies from goiters, apply moxibustion at Tianfu seven times, at Chongyang according to age.

Medical Case:
The "Ru Men Shi Qin" states: A woman from Xinzai, aged over forty, had a three-lobed goiter. She was instructed to induce vomiting with salt, which resulted in three expulsions, three sweats, and three bowel movements; her goiter was significantly reduced. Subsequently, she took medication to dissolve the goiter, leading to complete resolution. All ailments located above are suitable for purging; there are methods to gauge this as well.[60p]

　　戴人在西华，众人皆讪以为吐泻而已。一日，魏寿之与戴人入食肆中，见一夫病一瘤，正当目之上网内眦，色如灰李，下垂覆目睛，不能视物。戴人谓寿之曰：吾不待食熟立取此瘤。魏未之信也。戴人曰：吾与尔取此瘤如何？其人曰：人皆不敢割。戴人曰：吾非用刀割，别有术焉。其人从之，乃引入一小室中，令仰卧一床，以绳束其胻，刺乳中大出血。先令以手揉其目，瘤上亦刺出雀粪，立平出户。寿之大惊。戴人曰：人之有技，可尽窥乎？
　　郜城，戴人之乡也。一女子未嫁，年十八，两手背皆有瘤，一类鸡距，一类羊角。腕不能制，向明望之，如桃胶然。夫家欲弃之，戴人见之曰：在手背者为胶瘤，在面者为粉瘤。此胶瘤也。以(金非)针十字刺破，按出黄胶脓三两匙，立平，瘤核更不再作。婚事复成。非素明者，不敢用此法耳。[61p]

In Xi Hua, a healer was met with scorn from the crowd who believed he was merely vomiting. One day, Wei Shouzhi accompanied the healer to a food establishment, where they encountered a man suffering from a tumor located at the corner of his eye. It appeared gray and hung down over his vision, preventing him from seeing. The healer said to Shouzhi, "I won't wait for the food to cook; I will remove this tumor immediately." Wei was skeptical. The healer then proposed, "What if I take this tumor out for you?" The man replied that others had been too afraid to cut it. The healer insisted, "I won't use a knife; I have another technique." The man agreed and was led to a small room where he was instructed to lie supine on a bed, with his leg tied down. The healer then punctured the tumor, causing a significant amount of blood to flow. First, he massaged the man's eye; the tumor then expelled a clump of dark matter, and it was removed entirely. Shouzhi was astonished. The healer remarked, "Is it possible that a person with skill can be observed fully?"

In Gao City, which is the healer's hometown, there was an unmarried woman, eighteen years old, with tumors on both her hands that resembled chicken claws and ram's horns. Her wrists could not bend, and in the light of day, they appeared like peach gum. Her prospective husband's family wanted to abandon her, but the healer took a look and said, "The tumor on her hand is a gel tumor, and the one on her face is a powder tumor. This is a gel tumor." He used a specialized needle to break it open and squeezed out three spoonfuls of yellow gel-like pus, after which the tumor flattened and would not reappear. The marriage was back on. Only those lacking understanding would refrain from using this method.[61p]

　　《薛己医案》曰：长洲王天爵辛丑春，左腿环跳患瘤，状如大桃，按之濡软，恪服除湿流气化痰之剂，恶寒发热，食少体倦，形气俱虚，脉洪大而虚，气瘤也，肺主之。盖胆属木，肺属金，然发于胆经部分，乃肺金侮肝木，元气亏损，而其脓已内溃矣。遂用十全大补汤数剂，出清白稀脓甚多，顿加寒热，烦渴头痛，殊类伤寒状。余谓此因脓泄而血气益虚耳。仍用前汤，其势益甚，脉洪数大，按之如无，乃加附子一钱，其势愈甚而脉复如前，此虚甚而药未能及也。更加附子二钱，三剂诸证顿退。乃朝用补中益气汤，夕用十全大补汤，各三十余剂，出腐骨五块，疮口将完。后因不慎起居，患处复溃，诸证更发，咽间如焚，口舌无皮，用十全大补加附子一钱服之，诸证悉愈。二日不服，内病悉至，患处复溃。二年后又患，服前药不应，诊其尺脉，微细如丝，此属命门火衰，用八味丸为主，佐以十全大补汤，稍愈。至乙巳仍患虚寒之证而殁。[62p]

The "Medical Case of Xue Ji" states: In the spring of the Xin Chou year, Wang Tianjue of Changzhou suffered from a tumor on his left leg, shaped like a large peach, soft to the touch. He diligently took medicine to eliminate dampness, promote qi, and transform phlegm. He experienced chills, fever, decreased appetite, fatigue, and overall weakness; his pulse was robust yet vacuous, indicating a qi tumor associated with the lungs. Since the gallbladder relates to wood and the lungs to metal, the condition arose in the gallbladder meridian, where lung metal overcomes liver wood, leading to a depletion of original qi, and the pus had already festered internally.

He subsequently took several doses of the Ten Complete Tonifying Decoction, which expelled a considerable amount of clear, thin pus. However, his condition worsened, manifesting as chills and fever, intense thirst, and headache, resembling a typhoid state. I surmised that this was due to the pus draining out, further depleting his blood and qi. He continued taking the previous decoction, but his condition exacerbated with a pulse that was large and rapid, feeling as though there was nothing there. Thus, I added one qian of Fuzi (Aconite) to the prescription, yet the situation worsened and the pulse returned to its prior state, indicating an extreme deficiency beyond the medicine’s reach. I then increased the Fuzi to two qian, and after three doses, the symptoms diminished significantly.

In the morning, he took the Qi-tonifying Decoction, and in the evening, he took the Ten Complete Tonifying Decoction, each more than thirty doses, resulting in the expulsion of five pieces of necrotic bone, and the wound was nearly healed. Later, due to negligence in daily activities, the affected area festered again, and symptoms intensified. He experienced a burning sensation in his throat and had no skin on his lips and tongue. I prescribed the Ten Complete Tonifying Decoction with an addition of one qian of Fuzi, and all symptoms resolved. However, after two days without medication, the internal issues returned along with the festering.

Two years later, he suffered again, and the previous medication was ineffective. Upon examining his pulse, it was thin like a silk thread, indicating that the Mingmen fire had weakened. I prescribed the Eight Flavor Pill as the principal treatment, assisted by the Ten Complete Tonifying Decoction, which resulted in slight improvement. By the Yi Si year, he still suffered from symptoms of deficiency and cold, eventually passing away.[62p]

　　一男子左腿外侧近臀肿一块，上有赤缕三年矣。饮食起居如常，触破涌出血脓，发热恶寒，此胆经受证，故发于腿外侧。诊其脉，左尺洪数，右关弦洪，此肾水不能生肝木，用补中益气汤、六味地黄丸而痊。
　　一男子腹患瘤，脓水淋漓，此足三阴之证，用补中益气加麦门、五味以培脾土，用六味地黄丸以生肾水，更用芦荟丸以清肝火而敛。
　　一老儒眉间患瘤二年，其状如紫桃，下坠盖目，按之如水囊，此肝脾之证，脓瘀内溃而然耳。遂刺出血脓，目即开。以炒黑胆草、山栀、芎、归、芍药、柴胡、白朮、茯苓之类而愈。[63p]

A man had a swelling on the outer side of his left thigh near the hip, with a red thread for three years. His diet and daily activities were normal, but when it ruptured, blood and pus flowed out, causing fever and chills. This was a condition of the gallbladder meridian, hence it appeared on the outer side of the leg. Upon diagnosing his pulse, it was found to be forceful and rapid on the left wrist, and string-like and forceful on the right. This indicated that the kidney's water could not nourish the liver's wood. He was treated with Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang (Supplement the Middle and Benefit Qi Decoction) and Liu Wei Di Huang Wan (Six-Ingredient Pill with Rehmannia), resulting in recovery.

A man had a tumor in his abdomen, leaking pus and water. This indicated a condition of the three yin meridians. He was treated with an enhanced Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction with added Mai Men Dong (Ophiopogon), and Wu Wei Zi (Schisandra) to strengthen the spleen's earth, along with Liu Wei Di Huang Wan to generate kidney water. Additionally, Aloe Vera pills were used to clear liver fire and consolidate.

An elder scholar had a tumor between his eyebrows for two years, resembling a purple peach, hanging down over his eyes. When pressed, it felt like a water sac, indicating a condition of the liver and spleen, with internal pus and blood stasis. They proceeded to puncture it, releasing blood and pus, which immediately alleviated his vision. He was treated with ingredients such as fried black gallbladder herb, gardenia, ligusticum, angelica, peony, bupleurum, white atractylodes, and poria, leading to recovery.[63p]

　　嘉善周上舍两耳下项间，筋挛壅肿坚硬，咳嗽气喘，内热盗汗，所服皆化痰散坚行气之剂，势益甚。余诊之，左关弦濇，左尺洪数，此怒气伤肝，房劳损肾，须滋肾水，生肝血，慎调摄，至水旺之际，庶可愈矣。彼欲速效，乃外敷商陆、石灰等药，内服海藻、蓬朮之类，至秋金旺之际，元气愈虚，其肿愈甚而殁。
　　镇江孙上舍缺盆间肿如覆瓯，坚硬色赤，内热晡热，自汗盗汗，就治于余，曰：贱疾皆以散坚行气降火破血之剂，欲其内消而反甚。其脉左尺洪数，按之而弱，左关洪数，按之而濇，此怒气伤肝，血涸而筋挛也。因其急于仕进，余辞不能治。彼亦不信，后果殁。此证若补脾肺，滋肝肾，则木得水而敷华，筋得血而滋润，多有得生者。
　　府庠朱宏仁年二十，两手皆近中指患五疣，中一大者如黄豆，余皆如聚黍，拔之如丝，长三四寸许，此血燥筋缩，用清肝益荣汤五十余剂而愈。[64p]

In Jia Shan, a person named Zhou had a swelling between the ears and under the jaw, with hardened and congested muscles, coughing, and shortness of breath. They experienced internal heat and night sweats. The treatments they took were all aimed at resolving phlegm, dispersing hardness, and promoting the flow of energy, but their condition worsened. Upon examination, I found the left pulse weak and the left wrist pulse rapid, indicating that anger had harmed the liver and excessive work had damaged the kidneys. I advised nourishing kidney water and generating liver blood, and to be careful in regulating their activities. When water was abundant, it might lead to recovery. However, wanting quick results, they applied external medicinal pastes of herbs like smartweed and lime, and took internal remedies like seaweed and aconite. By autumn, as the elemental metal flourished, their vitality diminished further, leading to a worse swelling and eventual death.

In Zhenjiang, a person named Sun had a swelling between the legs resembling an overturned bowl, hard in texture and red in color, with internal heat and evening fevers, accompanied by spontaneous sweating and night sweats. They sought my treatment, stating that their ailment was being treated with remedies aimed at dispelling hardness, promoting energy flow, and reducing fire, but this only exacerbated their condition. Their left wrist pulse was rapid but weak, and the left pulse was rapid as well and hard upon pressure. This indicated that anger had harmed the liver, leading to blood depletion and muscle contraction. Due to their urgency for career advancement, I declined to treat them. They did not believe my warning and ultimately passed away. If this condition were treated by tonifying the spleen and lungs and nourishing the liver and kidneys, the wood would receive water and flourish, muscles would receive blood and moisten, leading to many surviving.

A student named Zhu Hongren, aged twenty, had five warts on each hand, with one large wart the size of a soybean, while the others resembled clusters of millet, pulling them off like silk and measuring about three or four inches in length. This indicated dried blood and contracted muscles. After treating with Qinggan Yirong Decoction for over fifty doses, he recovered completely.[64p]

　　府庠沈姬文幼嚙指甲，及长不能自禁。余曰：此肝火血燥也。又颈侧常生小疣子，屡散屡发；又臂生一块如菉豆大，若触碎如断束缕，扯之则长，纵之则缩，后两鬓发白点，求治。余曰：子素肝病，此部亦属肝胆经也。夫爪为筋之余，胆行人身之侧，正与嚙爪生疣等证相应，须滋补肾水以生肝胆，则诸病自愈矣。乃与六味地黄丸服之，二年，白点自退，疣亦不生。
　　一男子脸患疣，初如赤葚，杂用敷贴之药，翻张如菌；又用腐蚀，焮大如瘤。此足三阴经虚证悉具，治以补脾肺生肝肾等剂而寻愈。
　　一男子小腹中一块，不时攻痛，或用行气化痰等药不应。或以为血鳖，服行气逐血之剂，后手背结一肬子，渐长寸许，形如鳖状，肢节间如豆大者甚多。彼泥鳖生子发于外，亦用行血，虚证悉至，左尺洪数，关脉洪数弦。余以为肾水不能生肝木，以致肝火燥而筋挛，用六味地黄丸生肾水，滋肝血，三月余诸证悉愈。[65p]

In the government school, Shen Jiwen, as a child, used to bite her nails and, upon growing up, could not control it. I said: This is due to excess liver fire and blood dryness. Additionally, she often had small warts on the side of her neck that would repeatedly break out and then disappear; she also had a spot on her arm the size of a mung bean that seemed to break like fragile thread: if tugged, it would grow; if relaxed, it would shrink. Later, the hair at her temples turned white, and she sought treatment. I said: You have had liver issues; this region is also related to the liver and gallbladder channels. Nails are residues of tendons, and the gallbladder runs along the side of the body, which corresponds to the complaints of biting nails and warts; you need to nourish the kidney water to support the liver and gallbladder, and then all illnesses will heal. Thus, I gave her the Six-Flavor Rehmannia Pill. After two years, the white spots receded, and the warts no longer appeared.

One man had warts on his face that initially looked like red berries; after applying various ointments, they grew larger like fungi. Then he used caustics, and they expanded like tumors. This presented a complete deficiency of the three yin channels. I treated him with tonics for the spleen and lungs to nourish the liver and kidneys, and he soon recovered.

Another man had a spot in his lower abdomen that occasionally caused sharp pain. He tried using medications to move qi and dissolve phlegm, but they had no effect. He thought it might be related to blood clots and took qi-moving and blood-dispelling medicines. Later, a lump formed on the back of his hand that gradually grew to about an inch in size, resembling a turtle, with many small lumps appearing around his joints like mung beans. The mud turtle gives birth outward and requires blood-moving treatments. He had signs of deficiency, and his left wrist pulse was large, rapid, and string-like. I determined that the deficiency of kidney water was unable to nourish the liver wood, resulting in excess liver fire and muscle spasms. I prescribed the Six-Flavor Rehmannia Pill to generate kidney water and nourish liver blood, and after a little more than three months, all his symptoms had improved.[65p]

　　一男子因劳役过度，面色青黑，发热咳嗽，面生肬子，腹内一块，攻上攻下，作痛口干，小便秘濇，服消克之药愈甚。察其脉，左右关俱弦洪，元气弱甚，此肝脾受病而筋挛也。投以加味逍遥散，合地黄丸料，元气遂复。若误以为血鳖之类消之，必致不起。
　　一男子素膏粱醇酒，先便血便结，惊悸少寐，后肛门周生小颗如肬子，如鼠乳，大小不一，用清热消毒等药，半载之间，腿内股亦然。又用化痰之药，寒热吐痰，颈间俱作，肝肾脉浮数，按之而弱，余以为足三阴经血虚火炽，法当滋化源。彼不信，别服四物、黄蘗、知母之类，诸证蜂起，此胃气复伤，各经俱病也。先用补中益气汤三十余剂，诸证渐愈。乃朝用前汤，夕用八珍汤，又各五十余剂，诸证寻愈。于是夕改用六味丸加五味子，又半载诸证悉愈。[66p]

A man suffered from excessive labor, his complexion dark and sallow, experiencing fever and cough, with sores on his face and a lump in his abdomen, causing pain and dryness in his mouth, along with difficulty urinating. Taking medicines to resolve these issues only made his condition worse. Upon examining his pulse, it was found to be tight and forceful at both guan positions, indicating very weak vital energy, suggesting the liver and spleen were affected and the muscles were in spasm. He was given a modified Xiao Yao San combined with Di Huang Wan, which restored his vital energy. If he had mistakenly taken medications for blood stasis, his ailment would definitely have worsened.

Another man, who regularly consumed rich foods and strong liquor, initially experienced bloody stools and constipation, anxiety, and insomnia. Later, small lumps like warts appeared around his anal area, varying in size. After using medicines to clear heat and detoxify for six months, similar lumps appeared in his thighs. He used phlegm-relieving medicines, experiencing phlegm issues accompanied by cold and heat, and upon examining his liver and kidney pulses, they were fast and weak. I believed this was due to deficiency of blood and excess heat in the three yin meridians, and the method should nourish the source. He was skeptical and took Four Substance Decoction, Huang Lian, and Zhi Mu, leading to a resurgence of all symptoms, which damaged his stomach qi and affected all meridians. I first prescribed over thirty doses of Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang, and the symptoms gradually improved. He then took the same decoction in the morning and Ba Zhen Tang in the evening for over fifty doses, and the symptoms soon resolved. Eventually, in the evening, I changed to Liu Wei Wan combined with Wu Wei Zi, and after half a year, all symptoms were completely healed.[66p]

　　一妇人左手背并次指患五六枚，如熟葚，内热晡热，月经素不及期。余曰：此因肝脾血虚而有热也，当调补二经，使阴血生而诸证自愈。不信，乃用艾灸，手肿胀发热，手指皆挛，两胁项及胸乳间皆患疣，经行无期。余用加味逍遥散少加炒黑黄连数剂渐愈；乃去黄连，更佐以归脾汤，其患渐愈；又百余剂，经行如期；再用地黄丸三料而痊。
　　一妇小腹内一块，或时上攻，或时下坠，寒热胸痞，小便淋漓，或用行气化痰等剂，前证愈甚，月经两月余而一行；或以为内有肉鳖，啖饮其血而经不行，服驱逐之剂，下血甚多。两手背结一疣，如大豆许，两月渐长寸许，又两月余，又患数枚，疑以鳖子行于外，仍行驱逐。两耳下各患肿，又疑为疮毒。余曰：此属肝火血燥也，用加味逍遥、加味归脾二药兼服，佐以六味丸，三月余而愈。[67p]

A woman had multiple lesions on the back of her left hand and fingers, resembling ripe mulberries. She experienced internal heat and discomfort, with menstrual periods irregular and absent. I said this was due to deficiencies in the liver and spleen leading to heat. She should balance and nourish both channels, allowing the yin blood to grow, and then the symptoms would resolve on their own. Doubting this, she applied moxibustion, which caused swelling and heat in her hand, cramps in her fingers, and warts on her flanks, neck, and between her breasts, with menstruation still absent. I prescribed a modified version of Xiao Yao San with an added few doses of fried black Huang Lian, and she gradually improved. Then I removed Huang Lian and supplemented with Gui Pi Decoction, and her condition gradually got better. After about a hundred doses, her menstruation returned regularly. She then took three doses of Di Huang Wan and was cured.

Another woman had a mass in her lower abdomen, alternately causing upward pressure or downward heaviness, with chills and fever, chest tightness, and dribbling urination. I prescribed remedies to move qi and resolve phlegm, but these exacerbated her previous symptoms, resulting in over two months without menstruation. Some suspected there was a growth inside, and advised drinking its blood, leading her to take expelling remedies that caused significant blood loss. She had a wart on the back of each hand, each about the size of a large soybean, which grew to about an inch after two months, and she developed several more warts. Suspecting that the growths were linked to the external condition, I continued with the expelling treatments. She also developed swelling beneath both ears, suspected to be due to toxic sores. I concluded this was due to liver fire and blood dryness. I prescribed a combination of modified Xiao Yao and Gui Pi Decoction along with Liu Wei Di Huang Wan, and after more than three months, she was cured.[67p]

　　一妇人患疣，用蛛丝缠、芫花线、螳螂啖、毒药蚀、着艾灸，大溃肿痛，发热出血。余曰：此阴血虚也。不信，仍服降火之药而殁。
　　《外科正宗》曰：一男子臀瘤五年，形如覆瓢，按之隐隐黑色，此黑粉瘤也。以针破之，按出黑砂兼黑粉，共约碗许；用三品一条槍插入患内，十余日，每次捺出黑膜，其瘤渐消。内服十全大补汤，健脾胃，养气血，月余而敛。
　　一男子腮上生瘤半年，形若覆桃，皮色不变，按之微红，此粉瘤也。针破之，捺去脂粉，插前药，半月而愈。[68p]

A woman suffered from warts and used spider silk, Euphorbia, mantis bites, corrosive poison, and moxibustion, resulting in severe swelling and pain, fever, and bleeding. I said: This is due to a deficiency of Yin blood. She did not believe me and continued taking fire-reducing medicine, ultimately resulting in her death.

According to "The Authentic Text of External Medicine": A man had a tumor on his buttocks for five years, shaped like a covered gourd, which appeared dark when pressed. This was a black powder tumor. It was pierced with a needle, and dark sand and black powder were pressed out, amounting to about a bowl. A three-type needle was inserted into the affected area for over ten days, pressing out a black membrane each time, and the tumor gradually shrank. He also took a tonic soup to strengthen the spleen and stomach and nourish Qi and blood, and after a month, it healed.

A man developed a tumor on his cheek for six months, shaped like a covered peach, with unchanged skin color, which turned slightly red when pressed. This was a powder tumor. It was pierced with a needle to remove the fatty powder, and a front medication was inserted. It healed in half a month.[68p]

　　一义乌兵士，肩膊下连生小瘤五枚，三月余，渐发痒异状，以手扪之，内则噏噏攻动。余视之，内动果如虾。据此必有异虫。以针破其一枚，先出红水一匙，少顷，取出黑嘴粉红虫一枚，依然如旧，其人渐觉昏运，此泄气之过也。余瘤停止，服补中益气汤数剂，外以膏盖。又五六日，患者方健，渐渐破之，仍以补药十余服而愈。
　　一妇人并一女子，耳后发际下一寸各生一瘤，半年余，渐渐而大，此乃粉瘤。用针破之，先出脂粉，后出头发数根，长约二尺余，齐根剪断，出血少许，俱用插药，数日化出内膜而愈。以此观之，知有发瘤也。
　　一妇人腰间生一肉瘤，三年余，方渐微痛。一日溃后，出小蛔三条，长约五寸，置温汤中，游动半时方息。其时患者形体衰弱，面黄肌瘦，口干发热，朝以八味丸，午用人参养荣汤，服至百日外，元气渐醒；又百日，其口方收。余意度之，其蛔乃经络气血所化。[69p]

A soldier from Yiwu had five small tumors growing under his shoulder. After more than three months, they began to itch and felt unusual. When he touched them, he could feel something moving inside. Upon examination, it indeed felt like shrimp. Therefore, it was certain that there was an unusual insect inside. I used a needle to pierce one of the tumors, and initially, a spoonful of red fluid came out, followed shortly by a black-tipped pink worm, which was unchanged. The patient gradually felt weak, which was a consequence of the fluid loss. I stopped the tumor's growth, treated him with several doses of a tonic to replenish energy, and covered the area with an ointment. After five or six days, the patient felt better and gradually resumed breaking it down. I continued with a tonic of over ten doses until he recovered.

A woman and a girl each had a tumor about an inch below their hairline behind the ear, which had grown gradually for more than half a year. This was a fatty tumor. I used a needle to break it, and initially, fatty powder came out, followed by several strands of hair, each about two feet long, which I cut off at the roots. A little blood was lost, and I applied some medicine. Within several days, the inner membrane dissolved and they recovered. From this, it is evident that tumors can develop from hair.

Another woman had a flesh tumor on her waist for over three years, which had begun to ache slightly. One day, it burst, releasing three small roundworms about five inches long, which swam in warm water before stopping after a while. At that time, the patient looked weak, her face pale and thin, dry mouth and feverish. In the morning, she took Eight-Flavored Pills, and in the afternoon, Ginseng Nourishing Decoction. After taking it for about a hundred days, her vitality gradually revived; another hundred days passed before her mouth closed. I assessed that the worms were transformed from the energy and blood within the meridians.[69p]

　　一妇人气冲穴生瘤，红紫坚硬，乃血瘤也。请视之，心肝二脉俱洪数，其患得之心气郁结，肝气受伤之故。辞不可治。后请京师明公医治，其时头已穿溃，虽强投补托化坚凉血等剂，日溃日烂，终至不应。破经两月，一旦涌出紫血盆许，随即身亡。后人问曰：何以致此？余曰：心脉洪数，心火旺也。肝脉弦数，肝气伤也。火旺逼血妄行，肝气伤不能藏血，后破之必出血不止，多致危亡。预辞不治者，此意也。
　　《景岳全书》曰：余于三旬之外，忽于臀下肛门前，骨际皮里，生一小粒，初如菉豆许，不以为意，及半年而如黄豆矣，又一年而如皂子，复如栗矣。此时乘马坐椅，皆有所碍而渐至痛矣。然料此非敷药可散，又非煎药可及。使其日渐长大，则如升如斗，悬挂腰股间，行动不便，岂不竟成废人乎？抱忧殊甚。谋之识者，皆言不可割刺，恐为祸不小。余熟筹数月，莫敢妄动。[70p]

A woman developed a tumor on her body, red and purple, firm to the touch, which was identified as a blood tumor. Upon examination, both the heart and liver pulses were found to be strong and rapid, indicating that her condition was due to stagnation of heart energy and injury to liver energy. Treatment was deemed impossible. Later, she sought medical treatment in the capital, by which time the tumor had begun to ulcerate. Despite attempts to strengthen and cool her blood with various remedies, the ulcer worsened day by day, and ultimately, she did not respond to any further treatment. After two months of deterioration, a sudden gush of purple blood erupted, and she soon passed away. When later asked what caused this, I replied: the heart pulse was strong and rapid, indicating excess heart fire; the liver pulse was wiry and rapid, indicating liver injury. Excess heat forced the blood to flow erratically, while injured liver energy could not contain the blood, leading to uncontrolled bleeding when the tumor ruptured, often resulting in death. It was this reasoning that led me to advise against treatment.

In the "Complete Works of Jingyue," I noted that beyond three weeks, I suddenly felt a small lump beneath my buttocks, in front of the anus, beneath the skin near the bone, initially no larger than a mung bean. I paid it no mind, but after six months, it grew to the size of a yellow bean, and after another year, it resembled a soap nut, then grew to the size of a chestnut. At this point, sitting on a horse or in a chair became uncomfortable, and it gradually became painful. I recognized that this couldn’t be resolved with external ointments or herbal decoctions. If it continued to grow, it would reach the size of a compartment and hang between my waist and hips, severely limiting movement, which could potentially render me immobile. This caused me deep concern. Advisers warned against surgery, fearing significant complications. After contemplating for several months, I found no one who dared to act impulsively.[70p]

然窃计此时乘小不取，则日后愈大愈难矣，将奈之何？尝见人臀股间受箭伤者，未必即死，此之利害，不过如是，遂决意去之。一日，饮酒微醺，乘醉以柳叶针刺之，所出者皆如豆腐白皮之属，盖即粉瘤也。刺后顿消，余甚快然。及两日后，则肿如热痈，余以会通膏贴，三日脓溃而愈，余又快然。不两日，又肿起，更热更大，余则大惧大悔，谓瘤赘诚不可刺也。然无奈，复以会通膏贴之，又三日而大溃，出一囊如鱼胞者，然后收口全愈。今愈后数十年，此间仍有一小窍，诚险证也。向非余之勇决，则此后不知作何状；使开之再迟，则真有不可收拾者。是以病不早治，则不知所终，此亦可为治病者之鉴。
[71p]

I have secretly calculated that if I do not take action against this small issue now, it will only grow larger and harder to deal with in the future. What can be done about it? I have seen people who have been injured by arrows between their buttocks; they do not necessarily die from it. The pros and cons of this situation are somewhat similar, so I resolved to remove it. One day, feeling slightly tipsy from drinking, I took a willow needle and pierced it. What came out resembled the white skin of tofu, indeed, it was a small tumor. After piercing, it immediately shrank, and I felt quite pleased. However, two days later, it swelled like a hot abscess. I applied a medicated ointment, and after three days, it ruptured and healed, leaving me satisfied once more.

Yet, within two days it swelled again, hotter and larger, and I was filled with great fear and regret, believing that tumors should not be pierced. Nevertheless, I had no choice but to apply the medicated ointment again, and after another three days, it burst open, releasing something resembling a fish bladder, after which it closed up and fully healed.

Now, many years later, there remains a small pore, which is indeed a dangerous reminder. Had it not been for my decisive courage, I cannot imagine what might have happened later; had I delayed the procedure, it could have turned truly unmanageable. Thus, if a disease is not treated early, one cannot foresee the outcome; this serves as a lesson for those who treat illnesses.[71p]
